Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.\n                </span>\n                <small>\n                 <i>\n                  (March 2009)\n                 </i>\n                </small>\n                <small class="hide-when-compact">\n                 <i>\n                  (\n                  <a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">\n                   Learn how and when to remove this template message\n                  </a>\n                  )\n                 </i>\n                </small>\n               </div>\n              </td>\n             </tr>\n            </table>\n           </div>\n          </div>\n          <small class="hide-when-compact">\n           <i>\n            (\n            <a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">\n             Learn how and when to remove this template message\n            </a>\n            )\n           </i>\n          </small>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <b>\n        <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n         International Space Station\n        </a>\n        program\n       </b>\n       is tied together by a complex set of legal, political and financial agreements between the fifteen nations involved in the project, governing ownership of the various components, rights to crewing and utilization, and responsibilities for crew rotation and station resupply. These agreements tie together the five space agencies and their respective International Space Station Programs and govern how they interact with each other on a daily basis to maintain station operations, from traffic control of spacecraft to and from the station, to utilization of space and crew time. In spring 2010, the International Space Station Program Managers from each of the five partner agencies were presented with\n       <a href="/wiki/Aviation_Week" title="Aviation Week">\n        Aviation Week\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Laureate_Award&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Laureate Award (page does not exist)">\n        Laureate Award\n       </a>\n       in the Space category,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Aviation_Week_Laureate_Awards_1-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Aviation_Week_Laureate_Awards-1">\n         [1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and NASA\'s International Space Station Program was awarded the 2009\n       <a href="/wiki/Collier_Trophy" title="Collier Trophy">\n        Collier Trophy\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <table class="infobox" style="width:22em">\n       <caption>\n        International Space Station Program\n       </caption>\n       <tr>\n        <td <span class="toctext">\n             Utilization\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-4">\n         <a      <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-5">\n           <a href="#Expeditions">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             2.1\n            </span>\n            <span   <span class="tocnumber">\n             2.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Visiting spacecraft\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-7">\n           <a href="#Mission_control_centers">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             2.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Mission control centers\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-8">\n         <a href="#Commercial_Orbital_Transportation_Services">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           3\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Commercial Orbital Transportation Services\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-9">\n         <a href="#Constellation_Program">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           4\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Constellation Program\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-10">\n         <a href="#Future_of_the_ISS">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           5\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Future of the ISS\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-11">\n           <a href="#New_partners">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             5.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             New partners\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-12">\n         <a href="#Costs">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           6\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Costs\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13">\n           <a href="#NASA">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             NASA\n            </span>\n           </a>\n           <ul>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-14">\n             <a href="#2005_ISS_budget_allocation">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               6.1.1\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               2005 ISS budget allocation\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-15">\n             <a href="#Shuttle_costs_as_part_of_ISS_costs">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               6.1.2\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               Shuttle costs as part of ISS costs\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n            <li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-16">\n             <a href="#Post-Shuttle_ISS_supply_.26_costs">\n              <span class="tocnumber">\n               6.1.3\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               Post-Shuttle ISS supply &amp; costs\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n           </ul>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-17">\n           <a href="#ESA">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             ESA\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-18">\n           <a href="#JAXA">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             JAXA\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-19">\n           <a href="#Roskosmos">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.4\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Roskosmos\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-20">\n           <a href="#CSA">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.5\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             CSA\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21">\n         <a href="#Criticism">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           7\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Criticism\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22">\n         <a href="#End_of_Mission">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           8\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           End of Mission\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23">\n         <a href="#References">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           9\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           References\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24">\n         <a href="#External_links">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           10\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           External links\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_aspects">\n        Legal aspects\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Space_Station_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Legal aspects">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="1998_Agreement">\n        1998 Agreement\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Space_Station_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 1998 Agreement">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The legal structure that regulates the station is multi-layered. The primary layer establishing obligations and rights between the ISS partners is the Space Station Intergovernmental Agreement (IGA), an\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_treaty" title="International treaty">\n        international treaty\n       </a>\n       signed on January 28, 1998 by fifteen governments involved in the Space Station project. The ISS consists of Canada, Japan, the Russian Federation, the United States, and eleven Member States of the European Space Agency (Belgium, Denmark, France, Germany, Italy, The Netherlands, Norway, Spain, Sweden, Switzerland and the United Kingdom). Article 1 outlines its purpose:\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <i>\n        This Agreement is a long term international co-operative framework on the basis of genuine partnership, for the detailed design, development, operation, and utilization of a permanently inhabited civil Space Station for peaceful purposes, in accordance with international law\n       </i>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-legal_framework_2-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-legal_framework-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The IGA sets the stage for a second layer of agreements between the partners referred to as \'Memoranda of Understanding\' (MOUs), of which four exist between NASA and each of the four other partners. There are no MOUs between ESA, Roskosmos, CSA and JAXA because NASA is the designated\n       <i>\n        manager\n       </i>\n       of the ISS. The MOUs are used to describe the roles and responsibilities of the partners in more detail.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A third layer consists of bartered contractual agreements or the trading of the partners\' rights and duties, including the 2005 commercial framework agreement between NASA and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roskosmos" title="Roskosmos">\n        Roskosmos\n       </a>\n       that sets forth the terms and conditions under which NASA purchases seats on Soyuz crew transporters and cargo capacity on unmanned\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Progress_spacecraft" title="Progress spacecraft">\n        Progress\n       </a>\n       transporters.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A fourth legal layer of agreements implements and supplements the four MOUs further. Notably among them is the ISS code of conduct, setting out\n       <a href="/wiki/Criminal_jurisdiction" title="Criminal jurisdiction">\n        criminal jurisdiction\n       </a>\n       , anti-harassment and certain other behavior rules for ISS crewmembers.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">\n        <a href="#cite_note-3">\n         [3]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       made in 1998.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Utilization">\n        Utilization\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Space_Station_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Utilization">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       There is no fixed percentage of ownership for the whole space station. Rather, Article 5 of the IGA sets forth that\n       <i>\n        each partner shall retain jurisdiction and control over the elements it registers and over personnel in or on the Space Station who are its nationals\n       </i>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-legal_framework_2-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-legal_framework-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Therefore, for each ISS module only one partner retains sole ownership. Still, the agreements to use the space station facilities are more complex.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The station is composed of two sides:\n       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Orbital_Segment" title="Russian Orbital Segment">\n        Russian Orbital Segment\n       </a>\n       (ROS) and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Orbital_Segment" title="U.S. Orbital Segment">\n        U.S. Orbital Segment\n       </a>\n       (USOS).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Russian_side_4-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Russian_side-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         Russian Orbital Segment\n        </b>\n        (mostly Russian ownership, except the Zarya module)\n        <ul>\n         <li>\n          <i>\n           <a href="/wiki/Zarya" title="Zarya">\n            Zarya\n           </a>\n          </i>\n          : first component of the Space Station, USSR/Russia-built, U.S. funded (hence U.S.-owned)\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/Zvezda_(ISS_module)" title="Zvezda (ISS module)">\n           <i>\n            Zvezda\n           </i>\n          </a>\n          : the functional center of the Russian portion, living quarters, Russia-owned\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/Pirs_(ISS_module)" title="Pirs (ISS module)">\n           <i>\n            Pirs\n           </i>\n          </a>\n          : airlock, docking, Russia-owned\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/Poisk_(ISS_module)" title="Poisk (ISS module)">\n           <i>\n            Poisk\n           </i>\n          </a>\n          : redundancy for Pirs, Russia-owned\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/Rassvet_(ISS_module)" title="Rassvet (ISS module)">\n           <i>\n            Rassvet\n           </i>\n          </a>\n          : storage, docking, Russia-owned\n         </li>\n        </ul>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ISS_Hardware_Allocation.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="960" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/ISS_Hardware_Allocation.png/300px-ISS_Hardware_Allocation.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/ISS_Hardware_Allocation.png/450px-ISS_Hardware_Allocation.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/ISS_Hardware_Allocation.png/600px-ISS_Hardware_Allocation.png 2x" width="300"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ISS_Hardware_Allocation.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Allocation of the U.S. side of ISS hardware between nations.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         U.S. Orbital Segment\n        </b>\n        (mixed U.S. and international ownership)\n        <ul>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/Columbus_(ISS_module)" title="Columbus (ISS module)">\n           <i>\n            Columbus\n           </i>\n          </a>\n          : 51% for ESA, 46.7% for NASA and 2.3% for CSA.\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ESA-IGA_5-0">\n           <a href="#cite_note-ESA-IGA-5">\n            [5]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_Experiment_Module" title="Japanese Experiment Module">\n           <i>\n            Kib\xc5\x8d\n           </i>\n          </a>\n          : 51% for JAXA, 46.7% for NASA and 2.3% for CSA.\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JAXA-MOU_6-0">\n           <a href="#cite_note-JAXA-MOU-6">\n            [6]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          <a href="/wiki/Destiny_(ISS_module)" title="Destiny (ISS module)">\n           <i>\n            Destiny\n           </i>\n          </a>\n          : 97.7% for NASA and 2.3% for CSA.\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CSA-MOU_7-0">\n           <a href="#cite_note-CSA-MOU-7">\n            [7]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </li>\n         <li>\n          Crew time, electrical power and rights to purchase supporting services (such as data upload &amp; download and communications) are divided 76.6% for NASA, 12.8% for JAXA, 8.3% for ESA, and 2.3% for CSA.\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ESA-IGA_5-1">\n           <a href="#cite_note-ESA-IGA-5">\n            [5]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JAXA-MOU_6-1">\n           <a href="#cite_note-JAXA-MOU-6">\n            [6]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CSA-MOU_7-1">\n           <a href="#cite_note-CSA-MOU-7">\n            [7]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </li>\n        </ul>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Program_operations">\n        Program operations\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Space_Station_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Program operations">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Expeditions">\n        Expeditions\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Space_Station_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Expeditions">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_International_Space_Station_expeditions" title="List of International Space Station expeditions">\n        List of International Space Station expeditions\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Long-duration flights to the International Space Station are broken into expeditions. Expeditions have an average duration of half a year, and they commence following the official handover of the station from one Expedition commander to another. Expeditions 1 through 6 consisted of three-person crews, but the\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia_disaster" title="Space Shuttle Columbia disaster">\n        Space Shuttle Columbia disaster\n       </a>\n       led to a reduction to two crew members for Expeditions 7 to 12.\n       <a href="/wiki/Expedition_13" title="Expedition 13">\n        Expedition 13\n       </a>\n       saw the restoration of the station crew to three. While only three crew members are permanently on the station, several expeditions, such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Expedition_16" title="Expedition 16">\n        Expedition 16\n       </a>\n       , have consisted of up to six astronauts or cosmonauts. Only 3 members were active at any given time, one of the \'seats\' was rotated out during separate flights.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISSEx_8-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ISSEx-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-current_9-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-current-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-115" title="STS-115">\n        STS-115\n       </a>\n       expanded of the living volume and capabilities of the station so that it could host a crew of six. Expedition 20 was the first ISS crew of this size. Expedition 20\'s crew was lifted to the station in two separate\n       <a href="/wiki/Soyuz-TMA" title="Soyuz-TMA">\n        Soyuz-TMA\n       </a>\n       flights launched at two different times (each Soyuz-TMA can hold only three people):\n       <a href="/wiki/Soyuz_TMA-14" title="Soyuz TMA-14">\n        Soyuz TMA-14\n       </a>\n       on 26 March 2009 and\n       <a href="/wiki/Soyuz_TMA-15" title="Soyuz TMA-15">\n        Soyuz TMA-15\n       </a>\n       on 27 May 2009. However, the station would not be permanently occupied by six crew members all year. For example, when the Expedition 20 crew (\n       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Romanenko" title="Roman Romanenko">\n        Roman Romanenko\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Frank_De_Winne" title="Frank De Winne">\n        Frank De Winne\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Robert_Thirsk" title="Robert Thirsk">\n        Bob Thirsk\n       </a>\n       ) returned to Earth in November 2009, for a period of about two weeks only two crew members (\n       <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_Williams_(astronaut)" title="Jeffrey Williams (astronaut)">\n        Jeff Williams\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Maksim_Surayev" title="Maksim Surayev">\n        Max Surayev\n       </a>\n       ) were aboard. This increased to five in early December, when\n       <a href="/wiki/Oleg_Kotov" title="Oleg Kotov">\n        Oleg Kotov\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Timothy_Creamer" title="Timothy Creamer">\n        Timothy Creamer\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Soichi_Noguchi" title="Soichi Noguchi">\n        Soichi Noguchi\n       </a>\n       arrived on\n       <a href="/wiki/Soyuz_TMA-17" title="Soyuz TMA-17">\n        Soyuz TMA-17\n       </a>\n       . It decreased to three when Williams and Surayev departed in March 2010, and finally returned to six in April 2010 with the arrival of\n       <a href="/wiki/Soyuz_TMA-18" title="Soyuz TMA-18">\n        Soyuz TMA-18\n       </a>\n       , carrying\n       <a href="/wiki/Aleksandr_Skvortsov_(cosmonaut)" title="Aleksandr Skvortsov (cosmonaut)">\n        Aleksandr Skvortsov\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mikhail_Korniyenko" title="Mikhail Korniyenko">\n        Mikhail Korniyenko\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Tracy_Caldwell_Dyson" title="Tracy Caldwell Dyson">\n        Tracy Caldwell Dyson\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISSEx_8-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ISSEx-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-current_9-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-current-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The International Space Station is the\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_station#List_of_occupied_space_stations.2C_with_statistics" title="Space station">\n        most-visited spacecraft\n       </a>\n       in the history of space flight. As of 9 October 2015\n       <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=International_Space_Station_program&amp;action=edit">\n         [update]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       , The ISS has had 220 visitors.\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Mir" title="Mir">\n         Mir\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       had 137 visitors (104 different people).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SSSM_10-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-SSSM-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Visiting_spacecraft">\n        Visiting spacecraft\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Space_Station_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Visiting spacecraft">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_human_spaceflights_to_the_ISS" title="List of human spaceflights to the ISS">\n        List of human spaceflights to the ISS\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_unmanned_spaceflights_to_the_ISS" title="List of unmanned spaceflights to the ISS">\n        List of unmanned spaceflights to the ISS\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-118_approaching_ISS.jpg">\n         <img alt="A space shuttle, with its payload bay full of equipment, seen orbiting over a cloudy sky above a mountainous region of the Earth." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1005" data-file-width="1492" height="175" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/STS-118_approaching_ISS.jpg/260px-STS-118_approaching_ISS.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/STS-118_approaching_ISS.jpg/390px-STS-118_approaching_ISS.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/STS-118_approaching_ISS.jpg/520px-STS-118_approaching_ISS.jpg 2x" width="260"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS-118_approaching_ISS.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The\n         <span class="nowrap">\n          <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">\n           Space Shuttle\n          </a>\n         </span>\n         <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Endeavour" title="Space Shuttle Endeavour">\n          <i>\n           Endeavour\n          </i>\n         </a>\n         approaching the ISS during\n         <a href="/wiki/STS-118" title="STS-118">\n          STS-118\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Spacecraft from four different space agencies visit the ISS, serving a variety of purposes. The\n       <a href="/wiki/Automated_Transfer_Vehicle" title="Automated Transfer Vehicle">\n        Automated Transfer Vehicle\n       </a>\n       from the European Space Agency, the Russian Roskosmos Progress spacecraft and the\n       <a href="/wiki/H-II_Transfer_Vehicle" title="H-II Transfer Vehicle">\n        H-II Transfer Vehicle\n       </a>\n       from the Japan Aerospace Exploration Agency have provided resupply services to the station. In addition, Russia supplies a Soyuz spacecraft used for crew rotation and emergency evacuation, which is replaced every six months. Finally, the US serviced the ISS through its\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_program" title="Space Shuttle program">\n        Space Shuttle program\n       </a>\n       , providing resupply missions, assembly and logistics flights, and crew rotation until the program was retired in 2011.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX" title="SpaceX">\n        SpaceX\n       </a>\n       was the first private company to resupply the ISS\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">\n        <a href="#cite_note-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       in October 8, 2012.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The availability of docking ports on the station, and traffic from four different agencies and launch sites must be coordinated. Spacecraft launches can see delays while waiting for traffic to clear\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">\n        <a href="#cite_note-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A particular tight traffic jam occurred during the latch of ESA\'s Jules Verne\n       <a href="/wiki/Automated_Transfer_Vehicle" title="Automated Transfer Vehicle">\n        Automated Transfer Vehicle\n       </a>\n       in spring 2008. The cargo ship launched 2 day prior to\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-123" title="STS-123">\n        STS-123\n       </a>\n       , and had to wait in a holding orbit performing system tests while waiting for the shuttle to clear the station.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">\n        <a href="#cite_note-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       As of 13 April 2016\n       <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=International_Space_Station_program&amp;action=edit">\n         [update]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       , there have been 46 Soyuz, 63 Progress, 5 ATV, 5 HTV, 5 Cygnus, 7 Dragon and 37 Space Shuttle flights to the station.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISStD_14-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ISStD-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Expeditions require, on average, 2,722\xc2\xa0kg of supplies, Soyuz crew rotation flights and Progress resupply flights visit the station on average two and three times respectively each year.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Livelist_15-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Livelist-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       As of 13 April 2016\n       <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=International_Space_Station_program&amp;action=edit">\n         [update]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       , there were six spacecraft docked for the first time with the ISS:\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable">\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         Spacecraft\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         Mission\n        </th>\n        <th>\n UTC\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Progress_MS-1" title="Progress MS-1">\n          Progress MS-1\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         ISS Progress 62\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Pirs_(ISS_module)" title="Pirs (ISS module)">\n          Pirs\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mission_control_centers">\n        Mission control centers\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Space_Station_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Mission control centers">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mission_Control_Center" title="Mission Control Center">\n        Mission Control Center\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:888px;">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="">\n        <div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;">\n         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ISS_Centers.svg" title="Space centers involved with the ISS programme">\n          <img alt="A world map highlighting the locations of space centers. See adjacent text for details." data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="3388" height="260" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/ISS_Centers.svg/880px-ISS_Centers.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/ISS_Centers.svg/1320px-ISS_Centers.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/ISS_Centers.svg/1760px-ISS_Centers.svg.png 2x" width="880"/>\n         </a>\n        </div>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a href="/wiki/File:ISS_Centers.svg" title="File:ISS Centers.svg">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Space centers involved with the ISS programme\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The components of the ISS are operated and monitored by their respective space agencies at control centers across the globe, including:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        NASA\'s\n        <a href="/wiki/Christopher_C._Kraft_Jr._Mission_Control_Center" title="Christopher C. Kraft Jr. Mission Control Center">\n         Mission Control Center\n        </a>\n        at\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson_Space_Center" title="Lyndon B. Johnson Space Center">\n         Lyndon B. Johnson Space Center\n        </a>\n        in Houston, Texas, serves as the primary control facility for the US segment of the ISS and also controls the Space Shuttle missions that visit the station.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISSRG_16-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-ISSRG-16">\n          [16]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        NASA\'s\n        <a href="/wiki/Payload_Operations_and_Integration_Center" title="Payload Operations and Integration Center">\n         Payload Operations and Integration Center\n        </a>\n        at\n        <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Space_Flight_Center" title="Marshall Space Flight Center">\n         Marshall Space Flight Center\n        </a>\n        in\n        <a href="/wiki/Huntsville,_Alabama" title="Huntsville, Alabama">\n         Huntsville\n        </a>\n        , Alabama, serves as the center that coordinates all payload operations in the US Segment.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISSRG_16-1">\n         <a href="#cite_note-ISSRG-16">\n          [16]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        This center links Earth-bound researchers around the world with their experiments and astronauts aboard the International Space Station.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">\n         <a href="#cite_note-17">\n          [17]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Roskosmos\'s\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mission_Control_Center#RKA_Mission_Control_Center" title="Mission Control Center">\n         Mission Control Center\n        </a>\n        at\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Korolyov_(city)" title="Korolyov (city)">\n         Korolyov\n        </a>\n        , Moscow, controls the\n        <a href="/wiki/Russian_Orbital_Segment" title="Russian Orbital Segment">\n         Russian Orbital Segment\n        </a>\n        of the ISS, in addition to individual Soyuz and Progress missions.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISSRG_16-2">\n         <a href="#cite_note-ISSRG-16">\n          [16]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        ESA\'s\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Columbus_Control_Center" title="Columbus Control Center">\n         Columbus Control Center\n        </a>\n        at the\n        <a href="/wiki/German_Aerospace_Center" title="German Aerospace Center">\n         German Aerospace Center\n        </a>\n        (DLR) in\n        <a href="/wiki/Oberpfaffenhofen" title="Oberpfaffenhofen">\n         Oberpfaffenhofen\n        </a>\n        , Germany, controls the European\n        <i>\n         Columbus\n        </i>\n        research laboratory.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISSRG_16-3">\n         <a href="#cite_note-ISSRG-16">\n          [16]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        ESA\'s\n        <a href="/wiki/Automated_Transfer_Vehicle#ATV_Control_Centre" title="Automated Transfer Vehicle">\n         ATV Control Center\n        </a>\n        , at the\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toulouse_Space_Centre" title="Toulouse Space Centre">\n         Toulouse Space Centre\n        </a>\n        (CST) in\n        <a href="/wiki/Toulouse" title="Toulouse">\n         Toulouse\n        </a>\n        , France, controls flights of the unmanned European\n        <a href="/wiki/Automated_Transfer_Vehicle" title="Automated Transfer Vehicle">\n         Automated Transfer Vehicle\n        </a>\n        .\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISSRG_16-4">\n         <a href="#cite_note-ISSRG-16">\n          [16]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        JAXA\'s\n        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=JEM_Control_Centre&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="JEM Control Centre (page does not exist)">\n         JEM Control Centre\n        </a>\n        and\n        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=HTV_Control_Centre&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="HTV Control Centre (page does not exist)">\n         HTV Control Centre\n        </a>\n        at\n        <a href="/wiki/Tsukuba_Space_Center" title="Tsukuba Space Center">\n         Tsukuba Space Center\n        </a>\n        (TKSC) in\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tsukuba" title="Tsukuba">\n         Tsukuba\n        </a>\n        , Japan, are responsible for operating the\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_Experiment_Module" title="Japanese Experiment Module">\n         Japanese Experiment Module\n        </a>\n        complex and all flights of the unmanned Japanese\n        <a href="/wiki/H-II_Transfer_Vehicle" title="H-II Transfer Vehicle">\n         H-II Transfer Vehicle\n        </a>\n        respectively.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISSRG_16-5">\n         <a href="#cite_note-ISSRG-16">\n          [16]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        CSA\'s\n        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=MSS_Control&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="MSS Control (page does not exist)">\n         MSS Control\n        </a>\n        at\n        <a href="/wiki/Saint-Hubert,_Quebec" title="Saint-Hubert, Quebec">\n         Saint-Hubert\n        </a>\n        , Quebec, Canada, controls and monitors the\n        <a href="/wiki/Mobile_Servicing_System" title="Mobile Servicing System">\n         Mobile Servicing System\n        </a>\n        , or Canadarm2.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISSRG_16-6">\n         <a href="#cite_note-ISSRG-16">\n          [16]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_Orbital_Transportation_Services">\n        Commercial Orbital Transportation Services\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Space_Station_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Commercial Orbital Transportation Services">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Commercial_Orbital_Transportation_Services" title="Commercial Orbital Transportation Services">\n        Commercial Orbital Transportation Services\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       On January 18, 2006 NASA announced\n       <i>\n        Commercial Orbital Transportation Services\n       </i>\n       programme.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">\n        <a href="#cite_note-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       NASA has suggested that "Commercial services to ISS will be necessary through at least 2015."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">\n        <a href="#cite_note-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Instead of flying payloads to ISS on government-operated vehicles, NASA would spend $500 million (less than the cost of a single Space Shuttle flight) through 2010 to finance the demonstration of orbital transportation services from commercial providers.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       COTS must be distinguished from the related\n       <a href="/wiki/Commercial_Resupply_Services" title="Commercial Resupply Services">\n        Commercial Resupply Services\n       </a>\n       (CRS) program. COTS relates to the development of the vehicles, CRS to the actual deliveries. COTS involves a number of\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Act_Agreement" title="Space Act Agreement">\n        Space Act Agreements\n       </a>\n       , with NASA providing milestone-based payments.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On December 23, 2008, NASA entered into CRS contracts with\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orbital_Sciences" title="Orbital Sciences">\n        Orbital Sciences\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX" title="SpaceX">\n        SpaceX\n       </a>\n       to utilize their COTS cargo vehicles\xe2\x80\x94\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cygnus_spacecraft" title="Cygnus spacecraft">\n        Cygnus\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_Dragon" title="SpaceX Dragon">\n        Dragon\n       </a>\n       , respectively\xe2\x80\x94for cargo delivery to the International Space Station.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Constellation_Program">\n        Constellation Program\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Space_Station_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Constellation Program">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Constellation_Program" title="Constellation Program">\n        Constellation Program\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Constellation Program, a\n       <a href="/wiki/Human_spaceflight" title="Human spaceflight">\n        human spaceflight\n       </a>\n       program, was developed by NASA. On February 1, 2010, President\n       <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">\n        Barack Obama\n       </a>\n       announced a proposal to cancel the program effective with the\n       <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_federal_budget" title="2010 United States federal budget">\n        U.S. 2011 fiscal year budget\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_cancels_Moon_return_20-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BBC_cancels_Moon_return-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FY2011_budget_21-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-FY2011_budget-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WashPost_eliminates_funds_22-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-WashPost_eliminates_funds-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">\n        <a href="#cite_note-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       but later announced changes to the proposal in a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Barack_Obama_space_policy_speech_at_Kennedy_Space_Center" title="Barack Obama space policy speech at Kennedy Space Center">\n        major space policy speech\n       </a>\n       at Kennedy Space Center on April 15, 2010, which including reviving the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orion_(Constellation_program)" title="Orion (Constellation program)">\n        Orion capsule\n       </a>\n       for use as a rescue spacecraft for ISS.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Future_of_the_ISS">\n        Future of the ISS\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Space_Station_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Future of the ISS">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-globalize" role="presentation">\n       <tr>\n        <td class="mbox-image">\n         <div style="width:52px">\n          <img alt="Globe icon." data-file-height="290" data-file-width="350" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_globe_content.svg/48px-Ambox_globe_content.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_globe_content.svg/73px-Ambox_globe_content.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_globe_content.svg/97px-Ambox_globe_content.svg.png 2x" width="48"/>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n        <td class="mbox-text">\n         <div class="mbox-text-span">\n          The examples and perspective in this article\n          <b>\n           deal primarily with the United States and do not represent a\n           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Countering_systemic_bias" title="Wikipedia:WikiProject Countering systemic bias">\n            worldwide view\n           </a>\n           of the subject\n          </b>\n          .\n          <span class="hide-when-compact">\n           You may\n           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=International_Space_Station_program&amp;action=edit">\n            improve this article\n           </a>\n           , discuss the issue on the\n href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Article_wizard" title="Wikipedia:Article wizard">\n            create a new article\n           </a>\n           , as appropriate.\n          </span>\n          <small>\n
