href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">\n             Learn how and when to remove this template message\n            </a>\n            )\n           </i>\n          </small>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Heads_of_Agency_International_Space_Station.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3744" data-file-width="5616" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Heads_of_Agency_International_Space_Station.jpg/220px-Heads_of_Agency_International_Space_Station.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Heads_of_Agency_International_Space_Station.jpg/330px-Heads_of_Agency_International_Space_Station.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Heads_of_Agency_International_Space_Station.jpg/440px-Heads_of_Agency_International_Space_Station.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Heads_of_Agency_International_Space_Station.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The heads of the ISS agencies from Canada, Europe, Japan, Russia and the United States meet in Tokyo to review ISS cooperation.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Former\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NASA_Administrator" title="NASA Administrator">\n        NASA Administrator\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Michael_D._Griffin" title="Michael D. Griffin">\n        Michael D. Griffin\n       </a>\n       says the International Space Station has a role to play as NASA moves forward with a new focus for the manned space programme, which is to go out beyond Earth orbit for purposes of human exploration and scientific discovery. "The International Space Station is now a stepping stone on the way, rather than being the end of the line," Griffin said.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Explore_24-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Explore-24">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Griffin has said that station crews will not only continue to learn how to live and work in space, but also will learn how to build hardware that can survive and function for the years required to make the round-trip voyage from Earth to Mars.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Explore_24-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Explore-24">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Despite this view, however, in an internal e-mail leaked to the press on 18 August 2008 from Griffin to NASA managers,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-leak_25-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-leak-25">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-leak3_26-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-leak3-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-emailimage_27-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-emailimage-27">\n         [27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Griffin apparently communicated his belief that the current US administration had made no viable plan for US crews to participate in the ISS beyond 2011, and that the\n       <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Management_and_Budget" title="Office of Management and Budget">\n        Office of Management and Budget\n       </a>\n       (OMB) and\n       <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Science_and_Technology_Policy" title="Office of Science and Technology Policy">\n        Office of Science and Technology Policy\n       </a>\n       (OSTP) were actually seeking its demise.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-leak3_26-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-leak3-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The e-mail appeared to suggest that Griffin believed the only reasonable solution was to extend the operation of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_shuttle" title="Space shuttle">\n        space shuttle\n       </a>\n       beyond 2010, but noted that Executive Policy (i.e. the\n       <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">\n        White House\n       </a>\n       ) was firm that there will be no extension of the space shuttle retirement date, and thus no US capability to launch crews into orbit until the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ares_I" title="Ares I">\n        Ares I\n       </a>\n       /\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orion_(Constellation_program)" title="Orion (Constellation program)">\n        Orion\n       </a>\n       system becomes operational in 2014, at the earliest.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-leak3_26-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-leak3-26">\n         [26]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       He did not see purchase of Russian launches for NASA crews as politically viable following the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2008_South_Ossetia_war" title="2008 South Ossetia war">\n        2008 South Ossetia war\n       </a>\n       , and hoped the incoming\n       <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">\n        Barack Obama\n       </a>\n       administration would resolve the issue in 2009 by extending space shuttle operations beyond 2010.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A solicitation issued by NASA\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson_Space_Center" title="Lyndon B. Johnson Space Center">\n        JSC\n       </a>\n       indicates NASA\'s intent to purchase from Roscosmos "a minimum of 3 Soyuz seats up to a maximum of 24 seats beginning in the Spring of 2012" to provide ISS crew transportation.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">\n        <a href="#cite_note-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">\n        <a href="#cite_note-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On 7 September 2008, NASA released a statement regarding the leaked email, in which Griffin said:\n      </p>\n      <blockquote class="templatequote">\n       <p>\n        "The leaked internal email fails to provide the contextual framework for my remarks, and my support for the administration\'s policies. Administration policy is to retire the shuttle in 2010 and purchase crew transport from Russia until Ares and Orion are available. The administration continues to support our request for an\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/INKSNA" title="INKSNA">\n         INKSNA\n        </a>\n        exemption. Administration policy continues to be that we will take no action to preclude continued operation of the International Space Station past 2016. I strongly support these administration policies, as do OSTP and OMB."\n       </p>\n       <div class="templatequotecite">\n        \xe2\x80\x94\n        <cite>\n         Michael D. Griffin\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-leak2_30-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-leak2-30">\n           [30]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </cite>\n       </div>\n      </blockquote>\n      <p>\n       On 15 October 2008, President Bush signed the NASA Authorization Act of 2008, giving NASA funding for one additional mission to "deliver science experiments to the station".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-loc_31-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-loc-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-approve_32-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-approve-32">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Congress_Passes_Final_Version_HR6063_33-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Congress_Passes_Final_Version_HR6063-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-act2_34-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-act2-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Act allows for an additional space shuttle flight,\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-134" title="STS-134">\n        STS-134\n       </a>\n       , to the ISS to install the\n       <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Magnetic_Spectrometer" title="Alpha Magnetic Spectrometer">\n        Alpha Magnetic Spectrometer\n       </a>\n       , which was previously cancelled.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-obama1_35-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-obama1-35">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/President" title="President">\n        President\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">\n        Barack Obama\n       </a>\n       has supported the continued operation of the station, and supported the NASA Authorization Act of 2008.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-obama1_35-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-obama1-35">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Obama\'s plan for space exploration includes finishing the station and completion of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orion_Multi-Purpose_Crew_Vehicle" title="Orion Multi-Purpose Crew Vehicle">\n        <i>\n         Orion\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       spacecraft programme.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-obama2_36-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-obama2-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The operation of the ISS was prolonged until 2024.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="New_partners">\n        New partners\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Space_Station_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: New partners">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       China has reportedly expressed interest in the project, especially if it would be able to work with the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Federal_Space_Agency" title="Russian Federal Space Agency">\n        RKA\n       </a>\n       . However, as of 2009\n       <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">\n        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=International_Space_Station_program&amp;action=edit">\n         [update]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       China is not involved due to US objections concerning its human rights record and issues surrounding technology transfer.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-china_37-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-china-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">\n        <a href="#cite_note-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The heads of both the South Korean and Indian space agencies announced at the first plenary session of the 2009\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Astronautical_Congress" title="International Astronautical Congress">\n        International Astronautical Congress\n       </a>\n       on 12 October that their nations intend to join the ISS program. The talks begin in 2010, and were not successful. The heads of agency also expressed support for extending ISS lifetime.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISRO_and_KARI_to_join_ISS_39-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ISRO_and_KARI_to_join_ISS-39">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       European countries not a part of the International Space Station program will be allowed access to the station in a three-year trial period,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ESA" title="ESA">\n        ESA\n       </a>\n       officials say.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">\n        <a href="#cite_note-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Costs">\n        Costs\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Space_Station_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Costs">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       The most cited figure of an estimate of overall costs of the ISS ranges from 35 billion to 160 billion\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">\n        USD\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cost2_41-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-cost2-41">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       ESA, the only agency actually stating potential overall costs on its website, estimates\n       <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">\n        \xe2\x82\xac\n       </a>\n       100 billion.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-costs_42-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-costs-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Giving a precise cost estimate for the ISS is not straightforward, as it is difficult to determine which costs should actually be contributed to the ISS program, or how the Russian contribution should be measured.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="NASA">\n        NASA\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Space_Station_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: NASA">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NASA-Main_budget_chart_14-01-2004.svg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="673" data-file-width="898" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/NASA-Main_budget_chart_14-01-2004.svg/220px-NASA-Main_budget_chart_14-01-2004.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/NASA-Main_budget_chart_14-01-2004.svg/330px-NASA-Main_budget_chart_14-01-2004.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/NASA-Main_budget_chart_14-01-2004.svg/440px-NASA-Main_budget_chart_14-01-2004.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NASA-Main_budget_chart_14-01-2004.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         NASA\'s current budget projections see an end to ISS funding in 2017, in order to free funds for the\n         <a href="/wiki/Vision_for_Space_Exploration" title="Vision for Space Exploration">\n          Vision for Space Exploration\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The overall majority of costs for NASA are incurred by flight operations and expenses for the overall management of the ISS. Costs for initially building the U.S. portion of the ISS modules and external structure on the ground and construction in space as well as crew and supply flights to the ISS do account for far less than the general operating costs\n       <i>\n        (see\n        <a href="#2005_ISS_budget_allocation">\n         annual budget allocation below\n        </a>\n        )\n       </i>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       NASA does not include the basic Space Shuttle program costs in the expenses incurred for the ISS program, despite the fact that the Space Shuttle has been nearly exclusively used for ISS construction and supply flights since December 1998. NASA\'s 2007 budget request lists costs for the ISS (without Shuttle costs) as $25.6 billion for the years 1994 to 2005.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">\n        <a href="#cite_note-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       For each of 2005 and 2006 about $1.7 to 1.8 billion are allocated to the ISS program. The annual expenses will increase until 2010 when they will reach $2.3 billion and should then stay at the same level, however inflation-adjusted, until 2016, the defined end of the program. NASA has allocated between $300 and 500 million for program shutdown costs in 2017.\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="2005_ISS_budget_allocation">\n        2005 ISS budget allocation\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Space_Station_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: 2005 ISS budget allocation">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-114_Steve_Robinson_on_Canadarm2.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3032" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/STS-114_Steve_Robinson_on_Canadarm2.jpg/220px-STS-114_Steve_Robinson_on_Canadarm2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/STS-114_Steve_Robinson_on_Canadarm2.jpg/330px-STS-114_Steve_Robinson_on_Canadarm2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/STS-114_Steve_Robinson_on_Canadarm2.jpg/440px-STS-114_Steve_Robinson_on_Canadarm2.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS-114_Steve_Robinson_on_Canadarm2.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         NASA allocates about 125 million US dollars (\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USD" title="USD">\n          USD\n         </a>\n         ) annually to\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extra-vehicular_activity" title="Extra-vehicular activity">\n          EVAs\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The $1.8 billion expensed in 2005 consisted of:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">\n        <a href="#cite_note-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         Development of new hardware\n        </b>\n        : $70 million were allocated to core development, for instance development of systems like navigation, data support or environmental.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         Spacecraft Operations\n        </b>\n        : $800 million consisting of $125 million for each of software, extravehicular activity systems, and logistics and maintenance. An additional $150 million is spent on flight, avionics and crew systems. The rest of $250 million goes to overall ISS management.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         Launch and Mission operations\n        </b>\n        : Although the Shuttle launch costs are not considered part of the ISS budget, mission and mission integration ($300 million), medical support ($25 million) and Shuttle launch site processing ($125 million) is within the ISS budget.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         Operations Program Integration\n        </b>\n        : $350 million was spent on maintaining and sustaining U.S. flight and ground hardware and software to ensure integrity of the ISS design and the continuous, safe operability.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         ISS cargo/crew\n        </b>\n        : $140 million was spent for purchase of supplies, cargo and crew capability for\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Progress_spacecraft" title="Progress spacecraft">\n         Progress\n        </a>\n        and\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soyuz_spacecraft" title="Soyuz spacecraft">\n         Soyuz\n        </a>\n        flights.\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Shuttle_costs_as_part_of_ISS_costs">\n        Shuttle costs as part of ISS costs\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Space_Station_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Shuttle costs as part of ISS costs">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-125_EVA4_Working_inside_Hubble.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/STS-125_EVA4_Working_inside_Hubble.jpg/220px-STS-125_EVA4_Working_inside_Hubble.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/STS-125_EVA4_Working_inside_Hubble.jpg/330px-STS-125_EVA4_Working_inside_Hubble.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/STS-125_EVA4_Working_inside_Hubble.jpg/440px-STS-125_EVA4_Working_inside_Hubble.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS-125_EVA4_Working_inside_Hubble.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The only non-ISS-related Shuttle flight between 2005 and 2011 was a\n         <a href="/wiki/Hubble_Space_Telescope" title="Hubble Space Telescope">\n          Hubble Space Telescope\n         </a>\n         servicing mission on\n         <a href="/wiki/STS-125" title="STS-125">\n          STS-125\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Only costs for mission and mission integration and launch site processing for the 33 ISS-related Shuttle flights are included in NASA\'s ISS program costs. Basic costs of the Shuttle program are, as mentioned above, not considered part of the overall ISS costs by NASA, because the Shuttle program is considered an independent program aside from the ISS. Since December 1998 the Shuttle has, however, been used nearly exclusively for ISS flights (since the first ISS flight in December 1998, until October 2007 only 5 flights out of 28 flights have not been to the ISS, and only the planned\n       <a href="/wiki/Hubble_Space_Telescope" title="Hubble Space Telescope">\n        Hubble Space Telescope\n       </a>\n       servicing mission in 2009 will not be ISS-related out of 13 planned missions until the end of the Space Shuttle program in 2010).\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span id="Post-Shuttle_ISS_supply_&amp;_costs">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Post-Shuttle_ISS_supply_.26_costs">\n        Post-Shuttle ISS supply &amp; costs\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Space_Station_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Post-Shuttle ISS supply &amp; costs">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       The Space Shuttle was retired from service upon the conclusion of Atlantis\' final flight on July 21, 2011. NASA was reliant even at the time on some of the resupply contracts being fielded out to Soyuz and Progress and the other unmanned tugs, but it had launched a few years earlier into a program of aggressive development of commercial US resupply vehicles. At the beginning of 2014 both\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX" title="SpaceX">\n        SpaceX\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <a href="/wiki/SpaceX_Dragon" title="SpaceX Dragon">\n        Dragon\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Orbital_Sciences_Corporation" title="Orbital Sciences Corporation">\n        Orbital\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Cygnus_(spacecraft)" title="Cygnus (spacecraft)">\n        Cygnus\n       </a>\n       vehicles have fulfilled commercial resupply contracts, and NASA will be shifting to full-time reliance on these, and possibly in the medium-term future SNC\'s Dream Chaser and the NASA-developed Orion capsule.\n      </p>\n      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">\n       <tr>\n        <td class="mbox-image">\n         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg">\n          <img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/>\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td class="mbox-text">\n         <div class="mbox-text-span">\n          <b>\n           This section needs expansion\n          </b>\n          .\n          <small>\n           You can help by\n           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=International_Space_Station_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">\n            adding to it\n           </a>\n           .\n          </small>\n          <small>\n           <i>\n            (January 2014)\n           </i>\n          </small>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       On January 8, 2014, the White House announced that the ISS was having its funding extended from an outlook that ended in 2020 to at least 2024. An estimate was issued that it would cost $3B/year for 2012-2024, a substantial share of NASA\'s then-$17B budget.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="ESA">\n        ESA\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Space_Station_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: ESA">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Further information:\n       <a href="/wiki/European_contribution_to_the_International_Space_Station" title="European contribution to the International Space Station">\n        European contribution to the International Space Station\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       ESA calculates that its contribution over the 15 year lifetime of the project will be \xe2\x82\xac9 billion.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">\n        <a href="#cite_note-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Just the costs for the Columbus Laboratory tops more than \xe2\x82\xac1.4 billion (about $2.1 billion), including the money spent on the ground control infrastructure known as\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Columbus_Control_Center" title="Columbus Control Center">\n        Columbus Control Center\n       </a>\n       to operate it. The total development costs for\n       <a href="/wiki/Automated_Transfer_Vehicle" title="Automated Transfer Vehicle">\n        ATV\n       </a>\n       amount to approximately \xe2\x82\xac1.35 billion\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">\n        <a href="#cite_note-46">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and considering that each\n       <a href="/wiki/Ariane_5" title="Ariane 5">\n        Ariane 5\n       </a>\n       launch costs around \xe2\x82\xac150 million, each ATV launch will incur considerable costs as well.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The ISS has been far more expensive than originally anticipated. The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ESA" title="ESA">\n        ESA\n       </a>\n       estimates the overall cost from the start of the project in the early 1990s to the prospective end in 2017 to be in the region of\n       <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">\n        \xe2\x82\xac\n       </a>\n       100 billion (\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">\n        $\n       </a>\n       157 billion or\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.K." title="U.K.">\n        \xc2\xa3\n       </a>\n       65.3 billion).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-costs_42-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-costs-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="JAXA">\n        JAXA\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Space_Station_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: JAXA">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The development of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_Experiment_Module" title="Japanese Experiment Module">\n        Japanese Experiment Module\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japan_Aerospace_Exploration_Agency" title="Japan Aerospace Exploration Agency">\n        JAXA\n       </a>\n       \'s main contribution to the ISS, has cost about 325 billion yen (about $2.8 billion).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">\n        <a href="#cite_note-47">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In the year 2005, JAXA allocated about 40 billion yen (about 350 million USD) to the ISS program.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">\n        <a href="#cite_note-48">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The annual running costs for Japanese Experiment Module will total around $350 to 400 million. In addition JAXA has committed itself to develop and launch the\n       <a href="/wiki/H-II_Transfer_Vehicle" title="H-II Transfer Vehicle">\n        H-II Transfer Vehicle\n       </a>\n       , for which development costs total nearly $1 billion. In total, over the 24 year lifespan of the ISS program, JAXA will contribute well over $10 billion to the ISS program.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Roskosmos">\n        Roskosmos\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Space_Station_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Roskosmos">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       A considerable part of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Space_Agency" title="Russian Space Agency">\n        Russian Space Agency\n       </a>\n       \'s budget is used for the ISS. Since 1998 there have been over two dozen Soyuz and Progress flights, the primary crew and cargo transporters since 2003. The question of how much Russia spends on the station (measured in\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">\n        USD\n       </a>\n       ), is, however, not easy to answer. The two modules currently in orbit are derivatives of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Mir" title="Mir">\n        Mir\n       </a>\n       program and therefore development costs are much lower than for other modules. In addition, the exchange rate between ruble and USD is not adequately giving a real comparison to what the costs for Russia really are.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2010)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="CSA">\n        CSA\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Space_Station_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: CSA">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Canada, whose three main contributions to the ISS are the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadarm2" title="Canadarm2">\n        Canadarm2\n       </a>\n       , the mobile base system, and\n       <a href="/wiki/Dextre" title="Dextre">\n        Dextre\n       </a>\n       (the Special Purpose Dexterous Manipulator, also known as the Canada Hand), estimates that through the last 20 years it has contributed about\n       <a href="/wiki/Canadian_dollar" title="Canadian dollar">\n        C$\n       </a>\n       1.4 billion to the ISS. Canada has continued to be a vital member of ISS through the past ten years and continues to play a major role in the ISS.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">\n        <a href="#cite_note-49">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">\n        Criticism\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Space_Station_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Criticism">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n        International Space Station\n       </a>\n       has been the target of varied criticism over the years. Critics contend that the time and money spent on the ISS could be better spent on\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_versus_robotic_spaceflight" title="Human versus robotic spaceflight">\n        other projects\n       </a>\n       \xe2\x80\x94whether they be\n       <a href="/wiki/Robotic_spacecraft" title="Robotic spacecraft">\n        robotic spacecraft\n       </a>\n       missions,\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_exploration" title="Space exploration">\n        space exploration\n       </a>\n       , investigations of problems here on Earth, or just tax savings.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">\n        <a href="#cite_note-50">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Some critics, like\n       <a href="/wiki/Robert_L._Park" title="Robert L. Park">\n        Robert L. Park\n       </a>\n       , argue that very little\n       <a href="/wiki/Scientific_method" title="Scientific method">\n        scientific\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Research" title="Research">\n        research\n       </a>\n       was convincingly planned for the ISS in the first place.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">\n        <a href="#cite_note-51">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       They also argue that the primary feature of a space-based laboratory is its\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Microgravity_environment" title="Microgravity environment">\n        microgravity environment\n       </a>\n       , which can usually be studied more cheaply with a "\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vomit_Comet" title="Vomit Comet">\n        vomit comet\n       </a>\n       ".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">\n        <a href="#cite_note-52">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       One of the most ambitious ISS projects to date, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Centrifuge_Accommodations_Module" title="Centrifuge Accommodations Module">\n        Centrifuge Accommodations Module\n       </a>\n       , has been cancelled due to the prohibitive costs\n       <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">\n        NASA\n       </a>\n       faces in simply completing the ISS. As a result, the research done on the ISS is generally limited to experiments which do not require any specialized apparatus. For example, in the first half of 2007, ISS research dealt primarily with human biological responses to being in space, covering topics like\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kidney_stones" title="Kidney stones">\n        kidney stones\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Circadian_rhythm" title="Circadian rhythm">\n        circadian rhythm\n       </a>\n       , and the effects of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cosmic_rays" title="Cosmic rays">\n        cosmic rays\n       </a>\n       on the\n       <a href="/wiki/Nervous_system" title="Nervous system">\n        nervous system\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-renal_53-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-renal-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sleep_54-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sleep-54">\n         [54]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNS_55-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-CNS-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Other critics have attacked the ISS on some technical design grounds:\n      </p>\n      <ol>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Foust" title="Jeff Foust">\n         Jeff Foust\n        </a>\n        argued that the ISS requires too much maintenance, especially by risky, expensive\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extra-vehicular_activity" title="Extra-vehicular activity">\n         EVAs\n        </a>\n        .\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-foust_56-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-foust-56">\n          [56]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        The magazine\n        <i>\n         The American Enterprise\n        </i>\n        reports, for instance, that ISS astronauts "now spend 85 percent of their time on construction and maintenance" alone.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        The Astronomical Society of the Pacific has mentioned that its orbit is rather highly inclined, which makes Russian launches cheaper, but US launches more expensive.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-astrosoc_57-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-astrosoc-57">\n          [57]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        This was intended as a design point, to encourage Russian involvement with the ISS\xe2\x80\x94and Russian involvement saved the project from abandonment in the wake of the\n        <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia_disaster" title="Space Shuttle Columbia disaster">\n         Space Shuttle Columbia disaster\n        </a>\n        \xe2\x80\x94but the choice may have increased the costs of completing the ISS substantially.\n        <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n         [\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n           <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2011)">\n            citation needed\n           </span>\n          </a>\n         </i>\n         ]\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ol>\n      <p>\n       In response to some of these criticisms, advocates of manned space exploration say that criticism of the ISS project is short-sighted, and that manned space research and exploration have produced billions of dollars\' worth of tangible benefits to people on Earth. Jerome Schnee estimated that the indirect economic return from spin-offs of\n       <a href="/wiki/Human_spaceflight" title="Human spaceflight">\n        human space exploration\n       </a>\n       has been many times the initial public investment.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Schnee_58-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Schnee-58">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       A review of the claims by the Federation of American Scientists argued that NASA\'s rate of return from spin-offs is actually "astoundingly bad", except for aeronautics work that has led to aircraft sales.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fas_59-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-fas-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Critics also say that NASA is often casually credited with "spin-offs" (such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Velcro" title="Velcro">\n        Velcro\n       </a>\n       and portable computers) that were developed independently for other reasons.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">\n        <a href="#cite_note-60">\n         [60]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       NASA maintains a list of spin-offs from the construction of the ISS, as well as from work performed on the ISS.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spinoff_61-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-spinoff-61">\n         [61]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">\n        <a href="#cite_note-62">\n         [62]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       However, NASA\'s official list is much narrower and more arcane than dramatic narratives of billions of dollars of spin-offs.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2011)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       It is therefore debatable whether the ISS, as distinct from the wider space program, will be a major contributor to society. Some advocates argue that apart from its scientific value, it is an important example of international cooperation.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thirdanniv_63-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-thirdanniv-63">\n         [63]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Others claim that the ISS is an asset that, if properly leveraged, could allow more economical manned Lunar and Mars missions.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-marstoday_64-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-marstoday-64">\n         [64]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Either way, advocates\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch">\n          <span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (December 2011)">\n           who?\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       argue that it misses the point to expect a hard financial return from the ISS; rather, it is intended as part of a general expansion of spaceflight capabilities.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2011)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="End_of_Mission">\n        End of Mission\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Space_Station_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: End of Mission">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       In 2009, NASA had stated plans to end the ISS programme and\n       <a href="/wiki/Satellite#End_of_life" title="Satellite">\n        deorbit\n       </a>\n       the ISS in early 2016.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">\n        <a href="#cite_note-65">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This was in accordance with the then-President Bush\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Vision_for_Space_Exploration" title="Vision for Space Exploration">\n        policy\n       </a>\n       . President Obama announced new\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_policy_of_the_Barack_Obama_administration" title="Space policy of the Barack Obama administration">\n        policy\n       </a>\n       in 2010, extending the program through 2020.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NewBudget_66-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-NewBudget-66">\n         [66]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       All five ISS-participating space agencies had indicated in 2010 their desire to see the platform continue flying beyond 2015, but Europe struggled to agree on funding arrangements within its member states, until agreement was reached in March 2011.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2028_tokyo_67-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-2028_tokyo-67">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">\n        <a href="#cite_note-68">\n         [68]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">\n        <a href="#cite_note-69">\n         [69]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Russia and ISS partners in a 2011 statement said that work is being done to make sure other modules can be used beyond 2015. The first Russian module was launched in 1998, and the 30th anniversary of that module\'s launch has been chosen as a target date for certification of all components of the ISS.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2028_tokyo_67-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-2028_tokyo-67">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       According to a 2009 report,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RKK_Energia" title="RKK Energia">\n        RKK Energia\n       </a>\n       is considering methods to remove from the station some modules of the Russian Orbital Segment when the end of mission is reached and use them as a basis for a new station, known as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Orbital_Piloted_Assembly_and_Experiment_Complex" title="Orbital Piloted Assembly and Experiment Complex">\n        Orbital Piloted Assembly and Experiment Complex\n       </a>\n       (OPSEK). The modules under consideration for removal from the current ISS include the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Multipurpose_Laboratory_Module" title="Multipurpose Laboratory Module">\n        Multipurpose Laboratory Module\n       </a>\n       (MLM), currently scheduled to be launched mid-2018, along with other Russian modules which are currently planned to be attached to the MLM. Neither the MLM nor any additional modules attached to it would have reached the end of their useful lives by 2020. The report presents a statement from an unnamed Russian engineer who believes that, based on the experience from\n       <i>\n        Mir\n       </i>\n       , a thirty-year life should be possible, except for micrometeorite damage, because the Russian modules have been built with on-orbit refurbishment in mind.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RussiaSave_70-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-RussiaSave-70">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       According to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Outer_Space_Treaty" title="Outer Space Treaty">\n        Outer Space Treaty\n       </a>\n       the United States is legally responsible for all modules it has launched.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">\n        <a href="#cite_note-71">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In ISS planning, NASA examined options including returning the station to Earth via shuttle missions (deemed too expensive, as the station(USOS) is not designed for disassembly and this would require at least 27 shuttle missions\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">\n        <a href="#cite_note-72">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       ), natural orbital decay with random reentry similar to\n       <a href="/wiki/Skylab" title="Skylab">\n        Skylab\n       </a>\n       , boosting the station to a higher altitude (which would simply delay reentry) and a controlled targeted de-orbit to a remote ocean area.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISSEIS_73-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ISSEIS-73">\n         [73]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The technical feasibility of a controlled targeted deorbit into a remote ocean was found to be possible only with Russia\'s assistance.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISSEIS_73-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ISSEIS-73">\n         [73]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       At the time ISS was launched, the Russian Space Agency had experience from de-orbiting the\n       <a href="/wiki/Salyut_4" title="Salyut 4">\n        Salyut 4\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Salyut_5" title="Salyut 5">\n        5\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Salyut_6" title="Salyut 6">\n        6\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Salyut_7" title="Salyut 7">\n        7\n       </a>\n       space stations, while NASA\'s first intentional controlled de-orbit of a satellite (the\n       <a href="/wiki/Compton_Gamma_Ray_Observatory" title="Compton Gamma Ray Observatory">\n        Compton Gamma Ray Observatory\n       </a>\n       ) would not occur for another two years.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">\n        <a href="#cite_note-74">\n         [74]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       NASA currently has no spacecraft capable of de-orbiting the ISS at the time of decommissioning.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atvDeorbit_75-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-atvDeorbit-75">\n         [75]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Skylab" title="Skylab">\n        Skylab\n       </a>\n       , the only space station built and launched entirely by the US, decayed from orbit slowly over 5 years, and no attempt was made to de-orbit the station using a\n       <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_entry" title="Atmospheric entry">\n        deorbital burn\n       </a>\n       . Remains of Skylab hit populated areas of\n       <a href="/wiki/Esperance,_Western_Australia" title="Esperance, Western Australia">\n        Esperance, Western Australia\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-debris_76-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-debris-76">\n         [76]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       without injuries or loss of life.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       While the entire USOS cannot be reused and will be discarded, some Russian modules will be reused.\n       <a href="/wiki/Nauka_(ISS_module)" title="Nauka (ISS module)">\n        Nauka\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Uzlovoy_Module" title="Uzlovoy Module">\n        Node module\n       </a>\n       , two science power platforms and Rassvet, launched between 2010 and 2015 and joined to the ROS will be separated to form the next Russian space station\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/OPSEK" title="OPSEK">\n        OPSEK\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">\n        <a href="#cite_note-77">\n         [77]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="References">\n        References\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=International_Space_Station_program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: References">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n       <ol class="references">\n        <li id="cite_note-Aviation_Week_Laureate_Awards-1">\n         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">\n          ^\n          <a href="#cite_ref-Aviation_Week_Laureate_Awards_1-0">\n           <sup>\n            <i>\n             <b>\n              a\n             </b>\n            </i>\n           </sup>\n          </a>\n          <a href="#cite_ref-Aviation_Week_Laureate_Awards_1-1">\n           <sup>\n            <i>\n             <b>\n              b\n             </b>\n            </i>\n           </sup>\n          </a>\n         </span>\n         <span class="reference-text">\n          <cite class="citation web">\n           Michels, Jennifer (18 March 2010).\n           <a class="external text" href="http://www.aviationweek.com/aw/generic/story.jsp?id=news/awx/2010/03/18/awx_03_18_2010_p0-213236.xml&amp;headline=Aviation%20Week%202010%20Laureate%20Awards&amp;channel=defense" rel="nofollow">\n            "Aviation Week 2010 Laureate Awards"\n           </a>\n           .
